  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f972e43e-6832-490e-a204-02b16326af09'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText13274450689971366346" style="display:none">Montreal . . . the long, hot summer of 1996. . .<br /><br />. . . and in the dark of night, moving like a shadowy wraith, a vigilante prowls the city's streets.<br /><br />The targets of his bloody rampage: the worst of the worst.<br /><br />Murderers. Gangbangers. Rapists.<br /><br />Six months. Sixteen murders. The harried police are still without a clue . . .<br /><br />. . . until the day they receive an email from the assassin himself.<br /><br />Lieutenant Dave McCall, head of Montreal's Special Homicide Task Force, needs help to crack the secrets of the killer's taunting message. He calls on an expert--Chris Barry, who runs a security firm specializing in computer communications.<br /><br />Together, McCall and Barry launch a grim quest to track down a man who preys on predators--an urgent quest to bring this remorseless killer to justice.<br /><br />But whose justice will prevail: theirs--or the vigilante's?</span>

<div id="review_333423198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333423198" />
    <a title="Peter Carroll" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6397796-peter-carroll"><img alt="Peter Carroll" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442610348p2/6397796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333423198?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter Carroll" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter Carroll" href="/user/show/6397796-peter-carroll">Peter Carroll</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333423198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2059335312492875764">Three things made me read this book.<br/><br/>1. The author has a massive following on Twitter and blogs about Indie writing, handing out advice and tips.<br/><br/>2. The reviews are mostly gushing and fullsome in their praise.<br/><br/>3. It was available as a free download.<br/><br/>I have to admit to being ever so slightly disappointed. It's essentially a good story, well structured, with a few clever twists and touches, and he does a good job of juggling the possibilities and suspects. Unfortunately, I guessed the ending about hal</span>
  <span id="freeText2059335312492875764" style="display:none">Three things made me read this book.<br /><br />1. The author has a massive following on Twitter and blogs about Indie writing, handing out advice and tips.<br /><br />2. The reviews are mostly gushing and fullsome in their praise.<br /><br />3. It was available as a free download.<br /><br />I have to admit to being ever so slightly disappointed. It's essentially a good story, well structured, with a few clever twists and touches, and he does a good job of juggling the possibilities and suspects. Unfortunately, I guessed the ending about half way through so, for me, it was less revelatory than many other reviewers found it. That's not to say it is patently obvious (it's not) or that I am some kind of genius (as if!), I just thought it was good rather than gobsmacking.<br /><br />I didn't enjoy a lot of the dialogue. It tended to consist of the characters summarising or describing what had just occurred in the preceding chapter or paragraphs, which made me skim or ignore it. I also thought the description of tone, emotion and so on after each sentence uttered was overdone. <br /><br />I found the number of grammatical errors - a your instead of a you're for instance - and typos a bit off-putting. With modern electronic files, it is easy to go in and fix such things. This book is several years old and there are other reviews pointing out these glitches. Given the author's penchant for giving advice on writing, I think he should go back over the text and fix these. Don't get me wrong, it is not such a problem that it would spoil the read or the story, but it would improve it if he did.<br /><br />Overall, I would say it is worth reading and given that the vast majority of readers appeared to thoroughly enjoy it, my nit-picking is likely just that! I suspect my expectations were just a little too high going into it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2059335312492875764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_412267996" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412267996" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12678598-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347212141p2/12678598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412267996?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/12678598-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12678598-james?shelf=bad">bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12678598-james?shelf=bad-truly-awful">bad-truly-awful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412267996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10955139602127329161">Rarely have I read a novel so pitifully awful as Vigilante. If I were to write a detailed review of what Claude Bouchard got wrong, it would end up longer than the book itself. Instead, I'll stick with a few basic points.<br/><br/>1. The lead detective is pathetically inept, yet portrayed as a superstar. Now, this *can* actually work if you're making a more personal story focusing on character flaws, but the character portrayals in the book are delivered in such a shallow, "tell, don't show" style that it</span>
  <span id="freeText10955139602127329161" style="display:none">Rarely have I read a novel so pitifully awful as Vigilante. If I were to write a detailed review of what Claude Bouchard got wrong, it would end up longer than the book itself. Instead, I'll stick with a few basic points.<br /><br />1. The lead detective is pathetically inept, yet portrayed as a superstar. Now, this *can* actually work if you're making a more personal story focusing on character flaws, but the character portrayals in the book are delivered in such a shallow, "tell, don't show" style that it just comes off as jarring and annoying.<br /><br />2. The killer is unbelievably competent. Even a basic profile would have caught this guy early in the novel, but instead the police relied on techniques that have been outdated since the 80s. I'd make a joke about it being the Canadians, but Canadian police have been cutting edge long before American police.<br /><br />3. Horrible, horrible scene transitions and pacing. Every murder victim gets a long, dry, impersonal back-story and introduction so the author can tell you (again falling into the tell, don't show trap) that they're really bad and deserve to die. Every murder is sloppily written and performed in such a way that even 1996 forensics, which pre-dated widespread use of DNA, would have been able to figure this out.<br /><br />I've wasted enough time reviewing this awful novel. Read something else. Anything else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10955139602127329161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97469503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97469503" />
    <a title="Cari Foulk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3553085-cari-foulk"><img alt="Cari Foulk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1282919596p2/3553085.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97469503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15283051249224231104">You'd think, with years of editing fiction and reading countless queries and manuscripts, that I would be an expert at knowing who-done-it. Claude Bouchard has proven me wrong. I had NO idea what the outcome of this mind-bending mystery would be until the big reveal at the end of the novel. Not a clue! <br/>Brilliantly executed, sharp and concise writing, Vigilante is a stellar example of what a crime / mystery / thriller should be. Perfect. <br/>A must read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer299254119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6051809113023698997">This was my first book by this author but will not be my last, in fact I've already downloaded the next in this series. Maybe not 'quite' amazing but definitely my kind of book.<br/><br/>Fast pace, interesting characters and the author handled the vigilante theme very well, with enough of a twist to keep you involved. While I started to suspect the identity of the killer late in the book it certainly wasn't obvious and the entire plot was fast paced, with the actual killings handled with a relatively ligh</span>
  <span id="freeText6051809113023698997" style="display:none">This was my first book by this author but will not be my last, in fact I've already downloaded the next in this series. Maybe not 'quite' amazing but definitely my kind of book.<br /><br />Fast pace, interesting characters and the author handled the vigilante theme very well, with enough of a twist to keep you involved. While I started to suspect the identity of the killer late in the book it certainly wasn't obvious and the entire plot was fast paced, with the actual killings handled with a relatively light touch.<br /><br />My only reservation, if you can call it that, was that the finale seemed a little abrupt, with the "clearance" of the last two suspects somewhat abbreviated but it wasn't enough of a glitch to spoil my enjoyment of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6051809113023698997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16737687309973208742">Vigilante was my first step into the inspired world of Claude Bouchard. This spellbinding story kept me guessing until the very end. <br/><br/>A serial killer is busy with a variety of “projects”. You see, this serial killer is on a mission. He wants to rid Montreal of the vermin that keeps good people up at night. He exterminates a variety of criminals.   <span id="freeText16737687309973208742" style="display:none">Vigilante was my first step into the inspired world of Claude Bouchard. This spellbinding story kept me guessing until the very end. <br /><br />A serial killer is busy with a variety of “projects”. You see, this serial killer is on a mission. He wants to rid Montreal of the vermin that keeps good people up at night. He exterminates a variety of criminals. They are the lowlifes that we love to hate; pimps, rapists, drug dealers- you get the idea.<br /><br />Here is where conflict steps in. While most people feel that the Vigilante is doing good work, there is always that annoying legal issue. The police must find the killer. Moreover, to make it even more complicated, the killer is a likable guy!<br /><br />Law enforcement teams up with cutting edge technology and discover more than they bargained for. The storyline is brilliant. The characters are complex and you will immediately form strong feelings about each of them. However, will you be able to figure out the identity of the vigilante?<br /><br />I do not think so.<br /></span>

<div id="review_741830020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/741830020" />
    <a title="Jody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2506384-jody"><img alt="Jody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514381936p2/2506384.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/741830020?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody" href="/user/show/2506384-jody">Jody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506384-jody?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506384-jody?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506384-jody?shelf=kindle-fire">kindle-fire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer741830020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14042681792805037263">I received this book for free from a contest on simonjenner.com and I really enjoyed it. I like vigilante justice. I like Charles Bronson and Clint Eastwood and the idea that the law has failed us in respect to really putting away the guilty and so an ordinary man faces great obstacles and gets the justice he deserves. In Vigilante, the vigilante goes even further than exacting revenge for himself. He takes it upon himself to get revenge for those who have suffered at the hands of criminals. The</span>
  <span id="freeText14042681792805037263" style="display:none">I received this book for free from a contest on simonjenner.com and I really enjoyed it. I like vigilante justice. I like Charles Bronson and Clint Eastwood and the idea that the law has failed us in respect to really putting away the guilty and so an ordinary man faces great obstacles and gets the justice he deserves. In Vigilante, the vigilante goes even further than exacting revenge for himself. He takes it upon himself to get revenge for those who have suffered at the hands of criminals. There were no close calls, no near misses and no nail biting moments where it looks like the vigilante was outnumbered and about to be done in. There was simply straight forward action and adventure. There was great planning on the vigilante's part and there was some mystery in the book as to who was the real vigilante. Bouchard writes the story in a way that you think you know who the vigilante is but you keep second guessing yourself because of the plot turns. I can see where this book would leave those who are more liberal minded concerning crime and punishment upset thinking this book was full of hate and violence. I myself am more conservative and enjoy seeing the criminal "get what's coming to him" so to speak. If you are a fan of justice served up cold and calculating then you would enjoy this book and probably this whole series. I am glad I won this book and must say thank you to the author for writing it and to Simon Jenner for sponsoring this book as a "give away" on his website.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14042681792805037263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_574220795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574220795" />
    <a title="T.W. Barton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18846696-t-w-barton"><img alt="T.W. Barton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402687928p2/18846696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574220795?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.W. Barton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.W. Barton" href="/user/show/18846696-t-w-barton">T.W. Barton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574220795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1222860656382610177">I first read this book 3 years ago and loved it. I quickly bought the next 4 books in the series which I chewed through in over the next 3 weeks. I just started re-reading the series which is a mark for good books.<br/><br/>I'm a huge action/thriller fan and in particularly the vigilante genre. This book ticks all the boxes of what makes a good action/thriller book. Bad guys, cops, murder, and a vigilante.<br/><br/>I couldn't put this book down. Vigilante, Chris Barry is not some psychopathic serial killer. He's a </span>
  <span id="freeText1222860656382610177" style="display:none">I first read this book 3 years ago and loved it. I quickly bought the next 4 books in the series which I chewed through in over the next 3 weeks. I just started re-reading the series which is a mark for good books.<br /><br />I'm a huge action/thriller fan and in particularly the vigilante genre. This book ticks all the boxes of what makes a good action/thriller book. Bad guys, cops, murder, and a vigilante.<br /><br />I couldn't put this book down. Vigilante, Chris Barry is not some psychopathic serial killer. He's a very intelligent and likable guy. Oddly enough he's called in by the one person he should be avoiding at all costs, Lieutenant Dave McCall and you have to read to believe where that leads to.<br /><br />Who doesn't have a little vigilante in them? What draws me to the vigilante genre is the righting of wrongs when justice cannot or will not protect the people. Some of the series out there have characters that are clearly psychotic but choose to limit their victim pool to the filth of society. Then others, like this series, contain a character that could be the person next door. They participate in the community events, are well liked and respected. Little do we know that the danger lurking in the dark is really the champion of our safety and in turn the thing that goes bump in the dark for all those out there seeking to find a victim for their sick, perverse pleasures.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1222860656382610177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697926598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer825959007855592663">A serial killer is on the loose in Montreal but his sights are only set on criminals. But this is more than just a vigilante thriller - it is a cleverly woven mystery with plenty of red herrings thrown in along the way to torment the reader. We are pointed towards one suspect but doubts creep in as the story progresses. Although I had my suspicions as to the vigilante's identity, I wasn’t 100% sure who it was until the last sentence. As soon as I realised that the identity of the vigilante was a</span>
  <span id="freeText825959007855592663" style="display:none">A serial killer is on the loose in Montreal but his sights are only set on criminals. But this is more than just a vigilante thriller - it is a cleverly woven mystery with plenty of red herrings thrown in along the way to torment the reader. We are pointed towards one suspect but doubts creep in as the story progresses. Although I had my suspicions as to the vigilante's identity, I wasn’t 100% sure who it was until the last sentence. As soon as I realised that the identity of the vigilante was actually unknown, I was really drawn into the book. I couldn't put it down until I'd found out. I particularly enjoyed the pacing of this book as it interspersed the vigilante killings with back story and the progress of the investigation. While I did miss getting inside the head of the vigilante, although that would have given away the whole mystery part, the cleverly woven intrigue kept me reading well into the night.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10275162438544613450" style="display:none">I personally found the IDEA of a Vigilante STOPPING a crime before the victim is abused, punishing the criminal in a way that they will NEVER hurt anyone again, FASCINATING!<br /> <br />Cold Blooded Killer or Knight in Shining Armor?         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459089312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4831189022925210169">I read 'The Consultant', the second in Claude Bouchard's Vigilante series, a couple of months ago and gave it five stars at the time. I'm giving its predecessor, 'Vigilante', five stars too for exactly the same reasons. It's fast-paced, inventive, full of twists and turns, keeps you guessing and defies you to put it down. It also has the virtue of confronting the reader with a big moral dilemma. How do you feel about a killer who, on one hand, rids society of evil criminals but, on the other, do</span>
  <span id="freeText4831189022925210169" style="display:none">I read 'The Consultant', the second in Claude Bouchard's Vigilante series, a couple of months ago and gave it five stars at the time. I'm giving its predecessor, 'Vigilante', five stars too for exactly the same reasons. It's fast-paced, inventive, full of twists and turns, keeps you guessing and defies you to put it down. It also has the virtue of confronting the reader with a big moral dilemma. How do you feel about a killer who, on one hand, rids society of evil criminals but, on the other, does it by taking the law into his own hands?<br />Claude Bouchard's racy, exhilarating style keeps you hooked from first page to last. He is a highly skilled operator, a master of the thriller genre.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1191757136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191757136" />
    <a title="Carly Kirk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13567923-carly-kirk"><img alt="Carly Kirk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414964210p2/13567923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191757136?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carly Kirk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carly Kirk" href="/user/show/13567923-carly-kirk">Carly Kirk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10418071-vigilante">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191757136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9504416779249345204"><strong>Not too bad</strong><br/><br/>If I could, I would have given this 3 1/2 stars. It wasn't the best and it wasn't the worst crime/mystery I've read. The author tried for a twist ending, but something about the number of red herrings and the way they were written led me to figure out who the Vigilante was - and I'm not the type that usually even tries to figure that out.<br/><br/>I own the next two books in the series, so I'm going to read them and hope the author's writing grows a little more mature. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2101232870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2101232870" />
    <a title="DolphinBlue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22056650-dolphinblue"><img alt="DolphinBlue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507910440p2/22056650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2101232870?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DolphinBlue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DolphinBlue" href="/user/show/22056650-dolphinblue">DolphinBlue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2101232870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5151095797368065671">POSSIBLE SPOILER:<br/><br/>LOVED the surprise ending! The book was written in a tight (everything related to the plot), somewhat matter-of-fact style, which is not a criticism, just a comment. The reader really becomes invested in the outcome as the story progresses, and just when you think you have it figured out, BOOM, you find out you were wrong. I do want to go back and check to see whether the author cheated. The apparent solution was so obvious and spoon-fed, it will be interesting to see if the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText5151095797368065671" style="display:none">POSSIBLE SPOILER:<br /><br />LOVED the surprise ending! The book was written in a tight (everything related to the plot), somewhat matter-of-fact style, which is not a criticism, just a comment. The reader really becomes invested in the outcome as the story progresses, and just when you think you have it figured out, BOOM, you find out you were wrong. I do want to go back and check to see whether the author cheated. The apparent solution was so obvious and spoon-fed, it will be interesting to see if the storyline holds up under closer scrutiny, knowing the outcome. Regardless, it was a very fun read. It also had a subplot that was fun to follow. Recommended for mystery/suspense lovers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5151095797368065671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('u8Opf4pu6nfM0b7iuHzNFWcKTtLKyNh+oMbYrvmN20IwOc0SOb3ZTDq3SZlSfi3CNuog2tgOhewqz4kpTN1WPw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bDVgzrQiaiTfinHysP1AW/iQMZmHj/caLf0dYugsQvrnzwSjB/FZHynshola/6CMqXBfkZVJqoin9EzlXXzPhw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/579553.Claude_Bouchard">About Claude Bouchard</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/579553.Claude_Bouchard"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1250240398p3/579553.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10562682673856576706">*USA TODAY BESTSELLING AUTHOR*<br/><br/><br/>I was born in Montreal, Canada, at a very young age, where I still live with my spouse, Joanne, under the watchful eye of Krystalle and Midnight, two black females of the feline persuasion. In a former life, I completed my studies at McGill University and worked in various management capacities for a handful of firms for countless years. From there, considering my ext</span>
  <span id="freeText10562682673856576706" style="display:none">*USA TODAY BESTSELLING AUTHOR*<br /><br /><br />I was born in Montreal, Canada, at a very young age, where I still live with my spouse, Joanne, under the watchful eye of Krystalle and Midnight, two black females of the feline persuasion. In a former life, I completed my studies at McGill University and worked in various management capacities for a handful of firms for countless years. From there, considering my extensive background in human resources and finance, it was a logical leap in my career path to stay home and write crime thrillers.<br /><br />My first stab at writing was actually in 1995, the result being my first novel, "Vigilante". Two others of the same series followed by 1997 but all three remained dormant until publication in 2009. Since, besides writing a stand-alone, five other thrillers have joined the VIGILANTE series. I also penned "Something's Cooking", a faux-erotica parody and cookbook under the pseudonyms Réal E. Hotte and Dasha Sugah. I'm currently working on "See You in Saigon" and "The First Sixteen", two further installments of my series. I have to say, I'm enjoying this writing gig.<br /><br />Other interests besides writing and subtly persuading people to buy my books include reading, making noise with my six guitars, painting (oil and watercolour), cooking (year round though I love the grill in the summer), traveling and planning to work out soon. I've also been known to sleep on occasion.<br /><br />You can visit my website at claudebouchardbooks.com which is almost as fun as DisneyLand and absolutely free.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10562682673856576706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
